Endocytosis at the mouse blood brain barrier is elevated during sleep 1

2

Fu Li , Dechun Chen, Amita Sehgal 3

Howard Hughes Medical Institute and Chronobiology and Sleep Institute, 4

Perelman School of Medicine, University of Pennsylvania, Philadelphia, United 5

States 6

7

Abstract 8

Sleep is thought to be important for the clearance of brain waste , but exactly how it does 9

so is still debated . Here, we demonstrate that endocytosis in brain endothelial cells (BECs) 10 

of the blood –brain barrier (BBB) is enhanced during sleep, facilitating the removal of 11 

brain -derived waste, including amyloid -β, into the circulation. Using proteomics, in vivo 12 

tracer imaging, and endothelia l-specific genetic perturbations in mice, we demonstrate 13 

that sleep enhances endocytic vesicle formation and cargo transcytosis in brain 14 

endothelial cells (BECs) . Conversely , blocking endocytosis through endothelial Dnm2 15 

knockout suppresses BEC -mediated transport and elevates sleep need, revealing a 16 

causal feedback loop between sleep and vascular endocytosis. T hese findings identify 17 

BBB endocytosis as a key sleep -dependent clearance pathway with implications for 18 

neurodegenerative disease. 19 

Main 20 

Sleep is associated with improved cognition, synaptic plasticity and overall fitness. On a 21 

cellular/molecular level, work in Drosophila indicates that sleep maintains the integrity of 22 

neuronal mitochondria, at least in part by promoting the transfer of oxidative damage from 23 

neurons to glia 1. Other clearance functions attributed to Drosophila sleep, such as 24 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

autophagy and mobilization of lipids through the BBB, may also serve this goal 2 3. Indeed, 25 

efficient clearance of metabolic byproducts and misfolded proteins from the brain is critical 26 

for neuronal health across species . Impairment of waste clearance in mammals 27 

contributes to neurodegenerative diseases such as Alzheimer’s disease, in which 28 

amyloid -β (Aβ) and tau accumulate in the parenchyma 4. Glymphatic flow and meningeal 29 

lymphatic drainage have been implicated in clearance during sleep 5, but participation of 30 

the blood –brain barrier (BBB) remains unclear even though this clearly offers another 31 

mode of transport from the brain . Other than circadian and wake modulation of efflux 32 

transporters 6,7, regulation of the mammalian BBB has not been linked to sleep: wake 33 

states. 34 

Hypothesizing that the content and function of the BBB endothelium are modulated by 35 

sleep, we first sought to determine whether the protein profile of the endothelium is 36 

affected by sleep . We subjected one group of mice to 6 hours of sleep deprivation (SD) ,37 

starting at Zeitgeber Time (ZT0) or lights on, followed by 2 hours of recovery sleep, 38 

whereas a second group mice underwent 8 hours of SD (Fig. 1a ). Thus, they were 39 

collected at the same circadian time, and brain endothelial cells (BECs) were isolated 40 

from both groups. As we were particularly interested in proteins trafficked through the 41 

BBB, we extracted e ndosomal vesicles from these cells a nd analyzed proteins in these 42 

by Liquid Chromatograph y (LC) and a tandem mass spectrometer (MS/MS) method on 43 

QE -HF in DIA mode . A total of 2043 proteins were detected across all samples (Extended 44 

Data Table 1). Proteomic analysis of endosomes show ed that proteins involved in 13 45 

biological processes, 19 cellular components, and 16 molecular functions were 46 

significantly affected (Fig. 1d ). These proteins are involved in 10 functional pathways ,47 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

including translation complex formation and initiation as well as metabolism of polyamines, 48 

amino acids and derivatives. Eighteen proteins were higher in the group that was allowed 49 

to sleep (SD plus recovery) than the sleep -deprived (SD) group (Fig. 1b , c). Interestingly, 50 

this group included detectable level of Proteolipid protein 1 ( PLP1), which are unlikely to 51 

originate from endothelial expression. PLP1 is a major constituent of central nervous 52 

system (CNS) myelin, produced almost exclusively by oligodendrocytes, and is not 53 

expressed in vascular endothelial cells 8,9 . Its detection therefore most likely reflects 54 

uptake of myelin -derived vesicles or debris from the brain parenchyma . Although we 55 

cannot exclude the possibility that it represent s contamination of our samples, absence 56 

of other neuronal/glial proteins supports their active trafficking across the blood –brain 57 

barrier. Other proteins upregulated in the group allowed to sleep —Thumpd3, Dhx29, 58 

Ndor1, Tmed10, Prkra, Ube4b, Rpl22, Paip1, and Mtmr3 — are highly expressed within 59 

brain endothelial cells. Meanwhile,  26 proteins were lower in expression in the SD plus 60 

recovery group than in the control group. 61 

Given that PLP1 is not expressed in the BBB , we asked if it is trafficked to endothelial 62 

cells, perhaps to facilitate removal of excess protein. To investigate this, we 63 

overexpres sed GFP -tagged PLP1 in the brain and assayed for its presence in brain 64 

endothelial cells (BECs) . AAV -DJ -PLP1 -GFP was administered via 65 

intracerebroventricular (ICV) injection into the lateral ventricles of C57BL/6 mice to induce 66 

PLP1 expression in CNS parenchymal cells. As control, AAV -DJ -GFP was injected at the 67 

same location under identical conditions. AAV -DJ is a capsid variant with strong CNS 68 

tropism, often achieving higher transduction efficiency in the brain and spinal cord than 69 

natural serotypes such as AAV9 10 . As PLP1 has a long half -life (~100 days), we collected 70 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

mouse brains three months later to determine whether it had been transported to BECs. 71 

Confocal imaging revealed PLP1 -GFP signal in CD31 ⁺ BECs (Extended Data Fig. 1b , c),72 

suggesting transfer or uptake from surrounding parenchymal cells. Importantly, under 73 

identical conditions, AAV -DJ -GFP showed robust parenchymal expression but no 74 

detectable signal in BECs (Extended Data Fig. 1a , c), indicating that PLP1 localization is 75 

cargo -dependent rather than a result of direct viral transduction. These findings support 76 

a model in which PLP1 produced in parenchymal cells can be selectively internalized by 77 

the BECs .78 

To determine if similar changes occur with sleep in a daily cycle, we collected brain 79 

endothelial cells from mice at two time points, ZT8 ( sleep phase ) and ZT20 ( wake phase ).80 

Endosomes isolated from these cells were subjected to proteomic analysis using LC –81 

MS /MS . In total, 2,133 proteins were detected across all samples (Extended Data Table 82 

2). Among these proteins, 10 were specifically enriched in endosomes from mice in the 83 

sleep phase (Extended Data Fig. 3a , b). The most striking was the circadian and sleep -84 

associated regulator, growth hormone (Gh1) 11 , which showed a 90 -fold increase 85 

(Extended Data Fig. 3a , b). Another hormonal ly regulat ed molecule RACK1 12 was highly 86 

expressed as well. Additionally, several proteins involved in endocytosis and vesicle 87 

trafficking, such as Arhgef18 13,14 , Lrrk2 15,16 , Gripap1 17 , and FKBP15 , were upregulated 88 

between 2 - and 8 -fold. More interestingly, sleep phase BECs showed enrichment of 89 

metabolic and enzymatic components that regulat e endosomal metabolism , membrane 90 

lipid remodeling , PI (3)P and autophagy -related endosomes , namely Hdhd3, Lypla1, 91 

Mtmr3 and Ears2 respectively. When comparing SD+R with SD and ZT8 with ZT20, we 92 

found that a few proteins -RACK1 , Mtmr3 , Eef1g, Gars, Mtap, Prep, Rplp0 -were 93

It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

consistently enriched under sleep conditions ( SD+R and ZT8) . Actbl2 protein was 94 

upregulated in the SD+R group and downregulated in the ZT8 group , suggesting that it s95 

regulation is not strictly sleep -dependent . Taken together, these findings suggest a sleep -96 

specific endothelial program that enhances endocytosis and endosome maturation, 97 

raising the question of whether transport across the BBB is more active during sleep. 98 

Waste products resulting from tissue activity are often secreted in the form of extracellular 99 

vesicles, or exosomes. To determine if this occurred with sleep deprivation, we examined 100 

vesicular changes in the mouse brain. Following 6 hours of sleep deprivation, brains were 101 

harvested, fixed, and subjected to immunofluorescence staining for the exosome marker 102 

CD63 and the brain endothelial cell marker CD31 18,19 . Quantification revealed a103 

significant increase in CD63 -positive exosomes, indicating robust accumulation of 104 

exosomal vesicles after sleep deprivation (Extended Data Fig. 3c ). This accumulation 105 

suggests that sleep deprivation promotes the buildup of metabolic waste products or 106 

cellular debris, which are packaged and exported through exosomes. 107 

To obtain direct evidence that endocytosis is enhanced during sleep, we used 10 kDa 108 

dextran as a tracer to monitor trafficking from the brain through brain endothelial cells 109 

(BECs). To avoid sleep -like effects induced by prolonged anesthesia, dextran was 110 

delivered into the brain s of mice that had previously been cannulated via stereotaxic 111 

surgery . After a three -day recovery period following surgery , one set of mice underwent 6 112 

hours of sleep deprivation (SD) followed by 2 hours of recovery sleep, whereas another 113 

set was subjected to 8 hours of continuous SD. Dextran –Alexa Fluor ™ 488 was injected 114 

through the cannula into the second cortical layer (Fig. 2a ). Blood and brain tissue were 115 

collected 3 h after injection. The fluorescence intensity of dextran in the blood of SD plus 116 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

recovery mice was more than fivefold higher than in SD (Fig. 2e ). Consistently, 117 

immunostaining of brain sections revealed prominent colocalization of Dextran -488 with 118 

BECs in SD plus recovery mice but not in SD mice (Fig. 2b , c, d). 119 

To further confirm that brain endothelial cells (BECs) internalize dextran during sleep, we 120 

performed electron microscopy on mice subjected to the same treatment as in Fig. 1A. 121 

Electron micrographs revealed a marked increase in endocytic vesicles within BECs of 122 

experimental mice compared with controls (Fig. 2f –i). These vesicles frequently localized 123 

near the basolateral side , consistent with active uptake from the brain . Together, these 124 

findings provide ultrastructural evidence that endocytic activity in BECs is strongly 125 

enhanced during sleep. 126 

Although these data supported sleep -dependent endocytosis through the BBB , we sought 127 

to exclude other mechanisms that could account for the sleep -dependent dextran 128 

transport. Thus, we blocked endocytosis by downregulating Dynamin 2 (DNM2), a 129 

GTPase essential for vesicle scission during endocytosis and exocytosis 20 ,21 . For this 130 

purp ose, we used AAV -BR1 -Dnm2_K44A (encoding a dominant -negative DNM2 mutant 131 

fused to GFP ) where the BR1 serotype is a modified AAV2 variant with high specificity for 132 

the brain vascular endothelium 22,23 . The virus was delivered via tail vein injection, and 133 

then the mice were subjected t o cortical cannulation followed by injection of Dextran -594 .134 

Three hours after injection, at a time of high sleep (ZT8), blood dextran levels were more 135 

than fivefold higher in control mice than in Dnm2_K44A mutants (Fig. 3d ). Immunostaining 136 

further revealed that Dextran -594 colocalized with BECs in controls but not in 137 

Dnm2_K44A -expressing mice (Fig. 3a , b, c). T ogether these data indicate that blocking 138

It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

endothelial endocytosis suppresses both sleep -dependent dextran uptake by BECs and 139 

its clearance into the circulation .140 

We surmise that endocytosis from the brain through the BBB is promoted by sleep, and 141 

asked whether blocking it affects sleep amount. We allowed four weeks of expression of 142 

the AAV -BR1 -Dnm2_K44A , and then assessed sleep using the Piezo sleep monitoring 143 

system. Mice expressing Dnm2_K44A displayed significantly increased total sleep 144 

compared with wild -type Dnm2 controls (Fig. 3e , f). This is similar to what is seen in 145 

Drosophila 24 , and may indicate an increased need f or sleep when a function of sleep is 146 

compromised. 147 

To further validate the role of dynamin 2 in brain endothelial cells (BECs), we tried to 148 

knock out dynmin2 in BECs using a method described previously 6. However, we found 149 

that knockout of Dnm2 in BECs is developmentally lethal in mice . We thereby chose an 150 

alternate strategy in which we inject ed AAV -BI30 -Cre -GFP into Dnm2 flox/flox mice to 151 

selectively delete Dnm2 in the adult endothelium. AAV -BI30 is a capsid variant with high 152 

tropism for CNS endothelial cells and efficient penetration of the blood –brain barrier (BBB) 153 

> 25

. After 4 weeks, the loss of Dnm2 expression in BECs following knockout was confirmed 154 

by immunostaining ( Extended Data Fig. 5a, b). As before, we cannulated the mice and 155 

injected Dextran -647 at ZT5, during the sleep phase. Blood collected three hours later 156 

(ZT8) revealed markedly reduced fluorescence in Dnm2 knockout mice compared with 157 

controls (Fig. 3j). Immunostaining confirmed that Dextran -647 rarely entered BECs in 158 

knockout animals, whereas it was robustly internalized in controls (Fig. 3g, h, i). 159 

Conditional knockout of Dnm2 in BECs significantly increased total sleep time (Fig. 3k, l). 160 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

These results demonstrate that loss of Dnm2 attenuates endothelial endocytosis at the 161 

BBB, perhaps impairing transport from the brain and increasing sleep need. 162 

To determine whether endocytosis through the BBB has a diurnal rhythm , we first 163 

monitored sleep in C57BL/6 mice under LD12:12 conditions. As expected, mice 164 

predominantly slept around ZT2 and were largely awake at ZT14 (Fig. 4a). Accordingly, 165 

we injected Dextran -488 at ZT5 or ZT17 and collected blood and brains at ZT8 or ZT20 .166 

Fluorescence in the blood was dramatically higher at ZT8 than at ZT20 (Fig. 4e ), and 167 

Dextran -488 colocalization with BECs was likewise greater during sleep (Fig. 4b , c, d). 168 

Further evidence for this came from comparison of endocytosis at ZT2 and ZT 14 , with 169 

higher endo cytosis observed at ZT2. Thus, endocytosis at the BBB is enhanced during 170 

daily sleep, facilitating the transport of brain -derived substances into BECs and their 171 

subsequent release into circulation. 172 

Studies of clearance from the brain frequently examine the transport of Aβ 1-42 , which 173 

contributes to amyloid plaque formation in Alzheimer’s disease (AD) 26 . Thus, w e tested 174 

whether sleep -dependent endocytosis through the brain also mediates the clearance of 175 

Aβ 1–42 . Aβ 1–42 -488 was injected into the cortex at ZT5 or ZT17, and blood and brains were 176 

harvested at ZT8 or ZT20, respectively. Consistent with the tracer results, Aβ 1–42 -488 177 

levels were significantly higher in the blood at ZT8 than at ZT20 (Fig. 4i ), and localization 178 

in BECs was greater during the sleep phase (Fig. 4f , g, h). 179 

Although dynamin is considered a mediator of endocytosis, its loss also affects exocytosis 180 

by impeding vesicle trafficking. Our data suggest that endo and exocytosis are both 181 

important for sleep -regulated passage through the BBB. To specifically test for a role of 182 

exocytosis, we disrupted Exo70 , a core component of the exocytotic machinery 27,28 , in 183 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

BECs using CRISPR -Cas9. AAV -BI30 -saCas9 -GFP and AAV -BI30 -gRNA Exo70 were co -184 

administered via retro -orbital injection . The knockout of Exo70 in BECs was confirmed by 185 

immunostaining for Exo70 ( Extended Data Fig. 5c, d). Dextran -594 was infused at ZT5 186 

(sleep phase) using cannulation. Blood collected three hours later (ZT8) showed 187 

markedly reduced fluorescence in Exo70 knockout mice compared with controls 188 

(Extended Data Fig. 3d ). However, immunostaining demonstrated high accumulation of 189 

Dextran -594 within BECs of knockout mice, consistent with the idea that endocytosis is 190 

required for the uptake of dextran, and likely other material, from the brain but its release 191 

into the blood requires exocytosis (Extended Data Fig. 4a , b, c). As with the block in 192 

endocytosis, blocking exocytosis significantly increased sleep ( Extended Data Fig. 4e , f). 193 

194 

Together, these findings demonstrate that endo and exocytosis through the BBB occur 195 

during sleep, likely to clear waste from the brain . We previously demonstrated that the 196 

activity of efflux transporters in the BBB is regulated by a circadian clock in endothelial 197 

cells and is timed to occur during wake 6. Sang et al . subsequently replicated our findings 198 

and showed too that sleep deprivation enhances efflux, indicating that efflux does not just 199 

occur during wake but is promoted by it 7. Interestingly, Aβ removal through the BBB is 200 

thought to involve both low -density lipoprotein receptor -related protein 1 (LRP1) , which 201 

would act through an endocytic mechanism, as well as efflux transport 29,30 . Given that 202 

we saw higher endocytosis during sleep, we speculate that Aβ is taken up by BECs via 203 

endocytosis during sleep and its extrusion from these cells can occur via exocytosis or 204 

efflux. 205 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

Our findings establish a direct, causal link between sleep, endothelial endocytosis, and 206 

transport of material, likely waste, from the brain. Unlike glymphatic flow , which relies on 207 

CSF -ISF exchange , this pathway operates at the vascular interface, allowing metabolites 208 

to be rapidly sequestered from the parenchyma and exported into systemic circulation. 209 

The rhythmic upregulation of endocytic machinery (e.g., Arhgef18, Lrrk2) and hormonal 210 

signals (Gh1) during sleep suggests an active, rhythmic program for vascular 211 

detoxification. This may explain why chronic sleep disruption is a risk factor for 212 

Alzheimer’s disease: impaired BEC endocytosis could promote Aβ and tau accumulation 213 

unless com pl eme ntary enzymatic degradation mechanisms are engaged . PLP1 -GFP 214 

expressed in CNS parenchymal cells was detected in CD31 ⁺ brain endothelial cells 215 

(BECs), whereas GFP alone showed no endothelial signal, indicating cargo -dependent 216 

transfer or uptake. This suggests that PLP1 can move from parenchymal cells to the BBB, 217 

likely for its clearance . The observation that blocking BEC endocytosis increases sleep 218 

reveals a homeostatic feedback loop: when clearance is inefficient, the brain 219 

compensates by demanding more sleep. This positions the BBB not merely as a static 220 

barrier, but as a dynamic sensor and effector of brain metabolic state. Future work should 221 

explore whether enhancing BEC endocytosis pharmacologically or by promoting sleep 222 

can reduce amyloid burden or rescue cognitive deficits in neurodegenerative models. If 223 

so, targeting the vascular clearance axis may offer a novel therapeutic strategy — one 224 

that works with, rather than against, the brain’s natural rhythms. 225

Method 403 

Animal 404 

Male C57BL/6J mice were obtained from Jackson laboratory (#000664, 013542, Jackson 405 

lab). All mice were housed in a temperature -controlled facility maintained at 22 ± 1°C with 406 

a 12 -hour light/dark cycle (lights on at 07:00 and off 19:00 or lights on at 19:00 and off 407 

07:00) with free access to food and water and were 10 -12 weeks old at the time of surgery. 408 

All procedures were approved by Institutional Animal Care and Use Committees of the 409 

University of Pennsylvania and were done in accordance with the federal regulations and 410 

guidelines on animal experimentation (National Institutes of Health Offices of Laboratory 411 

Animal Welfare Policy). 412 

The B6.129S1(Cg) -Dnm2 tm1.1Pdc /J mice were obtained from Jackson laboratory (#013542, 413 

Jackson lab) and were born, bred and housed at University of Pennsylvania, Smilow 414 

Research Center of Translation animal facility. Breeding male and female B6.129S1(Cg) -415 

Dnm2 tm1.1Pdc /J mice and genotype offspring by PCR with the forward primer 5’ -416 

CCCTGCTAGTGACCTTTCTTGA -3’ and the reverse primer 5’ -417 

GCAGGAAGACACACAACTGAAC -3’. The Dnm2 fl/fl mice were injected the AAV -CAG -418 

Cre -GFP (AAV Serotype BI30) (SL116327, SignaGen Laboratories) to generate Dnm2 419 

knock outs specifically in BECs. All animals included in experiments were also included 420 

in data analysis and results. 421 

AAV -CAG -Dnm2 -GFP (AAV -BR1) and AAV -CAG -Dnm2_K44A -GFP (AAV -BR1) were 422 

produced by the Vector Core of the Gene Therapy Program, Perelman School of Medicine 423 

at the University of Pennsylvania. The viral titers were 1.73×10¹² and 2.54×10¹² PFU/mL, 424 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

respectively. Each virus was administered to 4 weeks old mice by retro -orbital injection 425 

using a total volume of 150 μL per animal. AAV -CAG -Exo70 -GFP (AAV -BI30) and AAV -426 

U6 -gRNA -CBh -mCherry (AAV -BI30) were produced following the method described by 427 

Negrini et al 31 . Viral titers, determined by qPCR, were 3.7×10¹² and 5.41×10¹² PFU/mL, 428 

respectively. Both vectors were delivered to 4 -week -old mice via retro -orbital injection at 429 

a total volume of 200 μL per animal (100 μL of each virus). 430 

An expression cassette encoding PLP1 alone was cloned into a pAAV -CAG -GFP transfer 431 

vector under the control of the CAG promoter. At the same time, pAAV -CAG -GFP empty 432 

vector was used the control vector. AAV -DJ particles were produced by co -transfecting 433 

the transfer plasmids with the pAAV -DJ capsid plasmid (#130878, Addgene) and helper 434 

plasmids in HEK293T cells. Viral titers, determined by qPCR, were 4.5×10¹² and 435 

4.34×10¹² PFU/mL, respectively. For in vivo experiments, C57BL/6 mice (4 weeks old) 436 

received intracerebroventricular (ICV) injections into the lateral ventricles under 437 

stereotaxic guidance. Each group containing 5 mice was injected with either AAV -DJ -438 

PLP1 -GFP or AAV -DJ -GFP at the same site (bregma as the 0 point: AP = -0.2 mm, ML 439 

= ±1.0 mm, DV = -2.2 mm) and under identical conditions to serve as experimental and 440 

control groups, respectively. 441 

442 

Isolation of brain endothelial cells (BECs) from mouse brain tissue 443 

All steps were performed on ice unless otherwise specified. Initially, 6 -well plates 444 

containing 6 -8 mL of complete media per well (RPMI -1640 (Life Tech, 11875093) were 445 

supplemented with 10% Newborn Calf Serum (Sigma, N4673 -500ML) and 1% Penicillin –446 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

Streptomycin (Life Tech, 15140 -122)). Mice were euthanized with 3 -5% Isoflurane, brains 447 

were rapidly dissected and immediately placed into ice -cold media. Using fine forceps, 448 

brain tissue was finely minced and transferred into a 50 -mL conical tube. To the minced 449 

tissue, we added Collagenase/Dispase (100 mg/mL stock in H ₂O) (Fisher, 17 -104 -019), 450 

200 μL of DNase I Grade II (1 mg/mL stock in H ₂O) (Sigma,10104159001), and 20 μL of 451 

Endosidin 2 (40 mM in DMSO) (Cayman, 21888). The total volume was brought to 20 mL 452 

with complete media. The suspension was incubated at 37°C with shaking at 250 rpm for 453 

20 minutes to facilitate tissue dissociation. While the tissue was digesting, a fresh 22% 454 

Percoll solution (Fisher, 45 -001 -748) was prepared for myelin and debris removal. To do 455 

this, a Percoll bottle was vortexed thoroughly, then 11 mL of Percoll was added to a 50 456 

mL conical tube, followed by 5 mL of 10×PBS and 34 mL of sterile water. Following 457 

thorough mixing, the solution was vacuum -filtered to remove particulates. Following the 458 

20 -minute digestion, the dissociated brain suspension was centrifuged at 500 × g (~1250 459 

rpm) for 5 minutes at 4°C. The supernatant was carefully aspirated and the pellet was 460 

resuspended in 1 mL of complete media (resulting in a total volume of approximately 2 461 

mL including the cell pellet). For myelin and debris removal, 4 mL of the freshly prepared 462 

22% Percoll solution was aliquoted into each of two 15 -mL conical tubes per brain. 1 mL 463 

of the resuspended brain slurry was transferred into each tube and centrifuged at 1000 × 464 

g for 10 minutes at 4°C. After centrifugation, a compact cell pellet forms at the bottom of 465 

the tube, while myelin and debris accumulate at the interface or top. The supernatant was 466 

carefully poured off and a pipette was used to remove any residual myelin or debris 467 

without disturbing the cell pellet. If the cell suspension was clumpy, it was passed through 468 

a 100 -μm cell strainer. Samples were pooled as needed (e.g., from multiple brains), then 469 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

5 mL of complete media was added and centrifuged again to pellet the cells. For positive 470 

selection of CD31 ⁺ endothelial cells, the final cell pellet was resuspended in 90 μL of PEB 471 

buffer (AutoRinse Buffer supplemented with BSA at a 1:20 dilution, stored at 4°C). 10 μL 472 

of CD31 MicroBeads (Miltenyi Biotec, 130 -097 -418) were added, mixed gently, and 473 

incubated on ice for 15 minutes. The MiniMACS Separator (Miltenyi Biotec, 130 -042 -102) 474 

was set up by placing an MS Column in the magnetic field. The column was pre -wet by 475 

rinsing it with 1 mL of PEB buffer. The labeled cell suspension was applied onto the 476 

column. The flow -through, which contains unlabeled (CD31 ⁻) cells, was collected. The 477 

column was washed with an additional 1 mL of PEB buffer and this effluent was collected 478 

as part of the CD31 ⁻ fraction. To recover the positively selected CD31 ⁺ cells, the column 479 

was removed from the magnetic separator and placed over a new collection tube. 480 

Immediately the column was flushed by applying 1 mL of PEB buffer and firmly pushing 481 

the plunger into the column to elute the magnetically retained CD31 ⁺ cells. This fraction 482 

represents the CD45 ⁻/CD31 ⁺ brain endothelial cell population. Finally, the isolated cells 483 

were counted. Typically, one sample consisting of pooled brains from five mice yields 484 

approximately 2 × 10⁶ CD31 ⁺ endothelial cells for proteomic analysis. 485 

486 

Endosome collection from the brain endothelial cells 487 

For endosomal proteins, brain endothelial cells were washed with cold PBS. The pellet 488 

was resuspended in 500 μl of Buffer solution of Minute Endosome Isolation (Invent 489 

biotechnologies, ED -028). The endosomal protein extraction was performed in 490 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

accordance with manufacturer instructions. The endosomes were collected and sent to 491 

the Children's Hospital of Philadelphia (CHOP) proteomics core for proteomic analysis. 492 

493 

Stereotaxic surgery and dextran injection 494 

To implant cannulae for dextran injection, mice were anesthetized with 3 -4% isoflurane 495 

and placed on a stereotaxic frame. The guide cannula (INC22 -1.5, World Precision 496 

Instruments) was inserted into the skull 1.2 mm from midline and 0.04 mm posterior to 497 

the bregma. The guide cannula was sticked to the skull with super glue and capped with 498 

a dummy cannula. After 3 days of the cannulation, 1 μl of 10000 Da dextran conjected 499 

with the Alexa Fluor 488 (D22910, Invitrogen) or the Alexa Fluor 594 (D22913, Invitrogen) 500 

or the Alexa Fluor 647 (D22914, Invitrogen) was injected into the mouse brain via a 501 

cannula by inserting into the internal cannula (INC22 -1.5, World Precision Instruments). 502 

503 

Sleep recordings 504 

Sleep of C57BL/6J, Dnm2 knockout, and Dnm2_K44A mutant mice was recorded in 505 

home cages to which animals had been habituated, under a 12 -h light/dark cycle (lights 506 

on at 07:00, off at 19:00). Sleep –wake states were monitored using a Piezo Adapt -A-507 

Base sensor (AAB -Sense; Signal Solutions) connected to a 16 -channel data acquisition 508 

system (16ch -DAQ; Signal Solutions). Sleep –wake classification was performed 509 

automatically using PiezoSleep 2.8 software and analyzed with SleepStats 2.18 (Signal 510 

Solutions). 511 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

512 

Blood fluorescent dextran measurement 513 

Blood was collected via cardiac puncture into 1 -mL lithium heparin –coated tubes 514 

(#450477, Greiner Bio -One). Samples were centrifuged at 2,000 × g for 20 min at 4 °C 515 

to obtain plasma. A 100 -μL aliquot of each plasma sample was transferred to a 96 -well 516 

plate, and fluorescence was measured at 488 or 647 nm by using a microplate reader 517 

(SpectraMax iD5, Molecular Devices). 518 

519 

Proteomics of endosomes 520 

Endosomal protein extracts were denatured, reduced, alkylated, and digested into 521 

peptides. The peptides were analyzed in single shot (per sample) on QE -HF in DIA mode 522 

by LC –MS/MS. Peptides were identified by using Spectronaut software (DIA, Biognosys) 523 

to compare with mouse reference proteome (25,125 entries, Reviewed canonical and 524 

isoforms). Perseus was used for statistical data analysis (peptides and proteins filtered at 525 

1% FDR; minimum 2 razor+unique peptides for protein quantification). Contaminants, 526 

reverse hits and proteins identified only by site were removed. LFQ intensities were log ₂527 

transformed. Differential abundance was assessed using a two -sample moderated t -test 528 

implemented in limma; p -values were adjusted by Benjamini –Hochberg (FDR). Proteins 529 

with |log ₂ fold change| ≥ 1 and FDR < 0.05 were considered significant. Heatmaps were 530 

generated from row -scaled log ₂ LFQ intensities (z -score per protein) and clustered by 531 

Euclidean distance with complete linkage. Volcano plots show log ₂ fold change versus 532 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

−log ₁₀ (FDR) with significant proteins highlighted. Functional enrichment on significant hits 533 

was performed using STRING or DAVID. All analyses and plotting were performed in R. 534 

535 

Electron -microscopy 536 

Following either 6 h of sleep deprivation plus 2 h of recovery or 8 h of continuous sleep 537 

deprivation, mice were deeply anesthetized and were fixed with 2.5% glutaraldehyde, 2.0% 538 

paraformaldehyde in 0.1M sodium cacodylate buffer, pH7.4, overnight at 4 ℃. After 539 

subsequent buffer washes, the samples were post -fixed in 2.0% osmium tetroxide for 1 540 

hour at room temperature, and rinsed in dH2O prior to en bloc staining with 2% uranyl 541 

acetate. After dehydration through a graded ethanol series, the tissue was infiltrated and 542 

embedded in EMbed -812 (Electron Microscopy Sciences, Fort Washington, PA). Thin 543 

sections were stained with uranyl acetate and lead citrate and examined with a JEOL 544 

1010 electron microscope fitted with a Hamamatsu digital camera and AMT Advantage 545 

NanoSprint500 software. Embedding, sectioning, and staining were performed by the 546 

Electron Microscopy Resource Laboratory at the University of Pennsylvania. 547 

Representative images were obtained from a single brain per group. All image analyses 548 

were performed blinded to experimental conditions. For vesicle quantification, vesicles or 549 

subcellular structures were counted per cell using Fiji/ImageJ. Statistical analyses were 550 

conducted on biological replicates (n values are indicated in figure legends) using 551 

unpaired t -tests as described in the main text. 552

Plasmid cloning 554 

For the AAV -CAG -Dnm2 -GFP and AAV -CAG -Dnm2_K44A -GFP plasmids construction, 555 

the coding region of the Dnm2 and Dnm2_K44A genes were amplified by PCR using RFP 556 

Dynamin2 Wild Type (#128152; Addgene) and RFP Dynamin2 K44A (#128153; Addgene) 557 

plasmids as templates and the forward primer 558 

‘AAATCTAGAATGGGCAACCGCGGGATGGAAG’ and the reverse primer 559 

‘AAAGGATCCGTCGAGCAGGGACGGCTCGGCT’. The PCR products were gel purified, 560 

digested with Xba I and BamHI, and ligated into the pAAV -CAG -GFP (#37825; Addgene) 561 

vector precut with the same enzymes. The AAV -CAG -saCas9 -GFP plasmid construction, 562 

the coding region of SV40 NLS, saCas9 and GFP genes were amplified by PCR using 563 

pSaCas9_GFP (#64709; Addgene) as template and the forward primer 564 

‘AAAGGATCCATGGCCCCGAAGAAAAA’ the reverse primer 565 

‘AAAAAGCTTTTACTTGTACAGCTCGT’. The PCR products were gel purified, digested 566 

with BamHI and HindIII, and ligated into the pAAV -CAG -GFP (#37825; Addgene) vector 567 

precut with the same enzymes. The guide RNA vector of Exo70 were generated by 568 

annealing the oligos ‘CACCCCTTG CTG TGC CGG GTCATC ’ and 569 

‘AAACGATGACCCGGCACAGCAAGG ’ and insert pSpCas9(BB) -2A -GFP (PX458) 570 

(#48138; Addgene) with the precut  BbsI (BpiI) sites. After the KO effect was confirmed in 571 

the Neuro -2a cells, the  guide RNA vector of Exo70 - pSpCas9(BB) -Exo70 -2A -GFP was 572 

subcloned into the pAAV -U6 -gRNA -CBh -mCherry (#91947; Addgene) with the NdeI sites. 573 

The cloning of mouse PLP1 gene by using the cDNA from Neuro -2a cell line with the 574 

forward primer ‘ ATG GGC TTGTTAGAGTGTTGT ’ and the reverse primer ‘ TCAGAA 575

578 

Histology for endocytosis 579 

Three hours after dextran injection, mice were deeply anesthetized and subjected to 580 

cardiac blood sampling. For histology of BECs, brains were fixed overnight in 4% 581 

paraformaldehyde (PFA) in PBS and then transferred to 30% sucrose in PBS solution for 582 

at least two night s. Brains were embedded and mounted with Tissue -Tek OCT compound 583 

(Sakura Finetek) and frozen. 20 μm sections were cut using a cryostat (CM3050, Leica) 584 

and mounted onto glass slides. Brain sections were washed in PBS, permeabilized using 585 

PBST (0.3% Triton X -100 in PBS) for 30 min and then incubated in blocking solution (3% 586 

normal calf serum (NCS) in PBST) for 1 h. Slices were then incubated in primary 587 

antibodies (1:200, anti -CD31 antibody, MA1 -26196, Invitrogen) overnight at 4 °C. 18 h 588 

later, slices were washed with PBS and incubated with the corresponding secondary 589 

antibody (1:1000, Alexa Fluor 594 - Highly Cross -Adsorbed Goat anti -Mouse IgG (H+L), 590 

A32742 or Alexa Fluor 647 - Highly Cross -Adsorbed Goat anti -Mouse IgG (H+L) A -21236 591 

Invitrogen). Brain sections were washed with PBS and mounted onto glass slides with 592 

mounting medium (#H1200, Vector Labs). Slides were cover -slipped with micro cover 593 

glass (#48404 -455, VWR). 594 

595 

Histology for knockout of Dynamin2 and Exo70 in BECs 596 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

Four weeks after injection of AAV -BI30 -Cre -GFP or AAV -BI30 -saCas9 together with AAV -597 

BI30 -gRNAEx070 -CBh -mCherry, experimental and control mice were deeply 598 

anesthetized, and brains were harvested. Brains were fixed overnight in 4% 599 

paraformaldehyde (PFA) in PBS, then transferred to 30% sucrose in PBS for at least two 600 

nights. Fixed brains were embedded in Tissue -Tek OCT compound (Sakura Finetek) and 601 

frozen. Coronal sections (20 μm) were cut using a cryostat (CM3050, Leica) and mounted 602 

onto glass slides. Sections were washed in PBS, permeabilized with PBST (0.3% Triton 603 

X-100 in PBS) for 30 min, and blocked in 3% normal calf serum (NCS) in PBST for 1 h. 604 

Slices were then incubated overnight at 4 °C with primary antibodies: anti -Dynamin2 (1:50, 605 

PA5 -29658, Invitrogen) or anti -Exo70 (1:100, 12014 -1-AP, Proteintech). After 18 h, 606 

sections were washed with PBS and incubated with secondary antibody (1:1000, Alexa 607 

Fluor 594 Highly Cross -Adsorbed Goat anti -Rabbit IgG (H+L), A32740, Invitrogen). Finally, 608 

sections were washed with PBS, mounted with medium (#H1200, Vector Labs), and 609 

cover -slipped with micro cover glass (#48404 -455, VWR). Loss of Dynamin2 or Exo70 610 

immunoreactivity in GFP brain endothelial cells was used to confirm efficient gene 611 

knockout. 612 

613 

Confocal microscopy of brain endothelial cells 614 

All fluorescent images of cells were acquired with an inverted Leica SP8 confocal 615 

microscope equipped with a motorized and piezo z stage, an HC PL APO CS2 40×/1.30 616 

oil -immersion objective (Leica Microsystems, Mannheim, Germany), Laser Diodes 405, 617 

488, 594, and 647, and HyD detectors. The settings for each image were Pinhole 1 Airy 618 

unit, 16 -bit acquisition, 4x zoom, 2048x2048 pixels field of view, 400 Hz scan speed, 619 

> .CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0 International license available under a was not certified by peer review) is the author/funder, who has granted bioRxiv a license to display the preprint in perpetuity. It is made The copyright holder for this preprint (which this version posted April 3, 2026. ;https://doi.org/10.64898/2026.04.02.716170 doi: bioRxiv preprint

resulting in a pixel size of 0.07 μm. All channels were detected on HyD detectors in 620 

multiple individual series to reduce bleed through: (1) Dextran (Alexa 488) and BECs 621 

(Alexa 594) channels (2) Dextran (Alexa 647) and BECs (Alexa 594) channels (3) AAV -622 

BI30 -Cre -GFP (Alexa 488) and Dextran (Alexa 594) channels (4) AAV -BI30 -saCas9 -GFP 623 

and Dextran (Alexa 594) channels (5) AAV -BI30 -Cre -GFP (Alexa 488) and Dynmin2 (Alex 624 

647) channels (6) AAV -BI30 -saCas9 -GFP and Exo70 (Alexa 594) channels detected. The 625 

detector gains and the laser intensity for the dextran (Alexa 488 or Alexa 647) channel 626 

were constant for all images acquired. Detector gains and laser intensities for the other 627 

channels were minimally adjusted between different plates and cell lines, if needed. 628 

629 

Image analysis 630 

Confocal micrographs of dextran and the BECs were selected randomly. After the 631 

background subtraction, using the BG Subtraction from ROI plugin of ImageJ software 632 

(version 1.44; National Institutes of Health), signal was quantified with the Intensity 633 

Analysis plug -in of ImageJ software. 634 

635 

Quantification and statistical analysis 636 

Sleep comparisons between control and experimental groups (Fig. 3 and Extended Data 637 

Fig. 4) were evaluated using Welch’s t-tests, unless otherwise specified in the figure 638 

legends. Comparisons of dextran fluorescence intensity in blood or brain endothelial cells 639 

(Figs. 2 –4) were analyzed using Mann –Whitney t-tests, as were comparisons of exosome 640 

numbers (Extended Data Fig. 1) and endosomal vesicle counts (Fig. 2h). All statistical 641

analyses were performed in GraphPad Prism. Detailed information on statistical tests, 642 

sample sizes, and significance thresholds is provided in the figure legends. 643
